## Instruction

Our coaching staff is currently working on season-long conditioning and rotation planning, with particular concern about ‚Äúback-to-back games‚Äù (cases where the same team plays on two consecutive days, with exactly 1 day apart between game dates). Hockey is extremely demanding, and if a season contains many back-to-back sets‚Äîespecially when the second game is often on the road‚Äîit can seriously impact player recovery and team performance.

Therefore, I‚Äôd like you to conduct a detailed analysis of the NHL 2024‚Äì2025 schedule (NHL 2024‚Äì2025 Schedule Data and calculate how many back-to-back sets each team will face this season. Please also break down, for each team, the number of occurrences in each of the four home/away configurations: Home‚ÄìAway (HA), Away‚ÄìHome (AH), Home‚ÄìHome (HH), and Away‚ÄìAway (AA). Note: Directly reading all content from the Google Sheet would be very lengthy.

Organize the results into a google spreadsheet named `nhl_b2b_analysis` under `NHL-B2B-Analysis` folder, and also save a local copy in the workspace as `nhl_b2b_analysis.csv`. The table headers should contain: `Team,HA,AH,HH,AA,Total`.

where Total represents the total number of back-to-back sets faced by each team across the season (i.e., the sum of HA, AH, HH, and AA).

This will make it easier for our coaches and data analysts to review and discuss later.

üßê`Agent`

Perfect! I can see the structure of the NHL schedule data. The columns are:
- Date (column A)
- Start Time (Sask) (column B)
- Start Time (ET) (column C) 
- Visitor (column D) - Away team
- Score (column E)
- Home (column F) - Home team
- Score.1 (column G)
- Status (column H)

Now I need to get all the data to analyze back-to-back games. Since the data is quite large (1315 rows), I'll fetch it in chunks and process it with Python.
</div>

<div className="tool-call-box">
<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"  viewBox="0 0 48 48" width="14px" height="14px" style={{margin: 0, padding: 0, display: 'inline-block'}}><path fill="#FFA000" d="M40,12H22l-4-4H8c-2.2,0-4,1.8-4,4v8h40v-4C44,13.8,42.2,12,40,12z"/><path fill="#FFCA28" d="M40,12H8c-2.2,0-4,1.8-4,4v20c0,2.2,1.8,4,4,4h32c2.2,0,4-1.8,4-4V16C44,13.8,42.2,12,40,12z"/></svg> `filesystem-write_file`

```text workspace/analyze_nhl_b2b.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
NHL Back-to-Back Games Analysis
Analyzes the 2024-2025 NHL schedule to identify back-to-back games for each team
"""

import json
import csv
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from collections import defaultdict

def parse_date_from_excel(date_value):
    """Convert Excel date serial number to datetime object"""
    if isinstance(date_value, (int, float)):
        # Excel date serial number (days since 1900-01-01, with 1900 incorrectly treated as leap year)
        base_date = datetime(1899, 12, 30)  # Excel epoch adjusted for the leap year bug
        return base_date + timedelta(days=date_value)
    elif isinstance(date_value, str):
        # Try to parse as date string
        try:
            return datetime.strptime(date_value, '%Y-%m-%d')
        except:
            return None
    return None

def analyze_back_to_back_games(schedule_data):
    """
    Analyze the schedule data to find back-to-back games for each team
    Back-to-back games are defined as games on consecutive days (exactly 1 day apart)
    """
    
    # Parse the schedule data
    games = []
    
    # Skip header row and process data
    for row_data in schedule_data[1:]:  # Skip header
        if not row_data or len(row_data) < 7:
            continue
            
        try:
            # Extract data from row
            date_val = row_data[0] if len(row_data) > 0 else None
            visitor = row_data[3] if len(row_data) > 3 else None
            home = row_data[5] if len(row_data) > 5 else None
            
            if not date_val or not visitor or not home:
                continue
                
            # Parse date
            game_date = parse_date_from_excel(date_val)
            if not game_date:
                continue
                
            games.append({
                'date': game_date,
                'visitor': visitor,
                'home': home
            })
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error processing row: {e}")
            continue
    
    # Sort games by date
    games.sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])
    
    # Create team schedules
    team_schedules = defaultdict(list)
    
    for game in games:
        # Add game to visitor team's schedule (away game)
        team_schedules[game['visitor']].append({
            'date': game['date'],
            'location': 'away',
            'opponent': game['home']
        })
        
        # Add game to home team's schedule (home game)
        team_schedules[game['home']].append({
            'date': game['date'],
            'location': 'home',
            'opponent': game['visitor']
        })
    
    # Sort each team's schedule by date
    for team in team_schedules:
        team_schedules[team].sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])
    
    # Find back-to-back games for each team
    b2b_analysis = {}
    
    for team, schedule in team_schedules.items():
        b2b_sets = {
            'HA': 0,  # Home-Away
            'AH': 0,  # Away-Home
            'HH': 0,  # Home-Home
            'AA': 0   # Away-Away
        }
        
        # Check consecutive games
        for i in range(len(schedule) - 1):
            current_game = schedule[i]
            next_game = schedule[i + 1]
            
            # Check if games are on consecutive days (exactly 1 day apart)
            date_diff = (next_game['date'] - current_game['date']).days
            
            if date_diff == 1:  # Back-to-back games
                # Determine the configuration
                current_loc = current_game['location'][0].upper()  # 'H' or 'A'
                next_loc = next_game['location'][0].upper()        # 'H' or 'A'
                
                config = current_loc + next_loc
                if config in b2b_sets:
                    b2b_sets[config] += 1
        
        # Calculate total
        total_b2b = sum(b2b_sets.values())
        
        b2b_analysis[team] = {
            'HA': b2b_sets['HA'],
            'AH': b2b_sets['AH'], 
            'HH': b2b_sets['HH'],
            'AA': b2b_sets['AA'],
            'Total': total_b2b
        }
    
    return b2b_analysis

def save_results_to_csv(analysis_results, filename):
    """Save the analysis results to a CSV file"""
    
    # Sort teams alphabetically
    sorted_teams = sorted(analysis_results.keys())
    
    with open(filename, 'w', newline='', encoding='utf-8') as csvfile:
        fieldnames = ['Team', 'HA', 'AH', 'HH', 'AA', 'Total']
        writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
        
        writer.writeheader()
        for team in sorted_teams:
            row = {'Team': team}
            row.update(analysis_results[team])
            writer.writerow(row)
    
    print(f"Results saved to {filename}")

def main():
    # Load the schedule data from the overlong tool output file
    try:
        with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/3AtEFGDSbdso7ftvnNzvnJ.json', 'r') as f:
            data = json.load(f)
        
        # Extract the sheet data
        sheet_data = data['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']
        
        # Convert to simple format for processing
        schedule_data = []
        for row in sheet_data:
            row_values = []
            if 'values' in row:
                for cell in row['values']:
                    if 'effectiveValue' in cell:
                        if 'numberValue' in cell['effectiveValue']:
                            row_values.append(cell['effectiveValue']['numberValue'])
                        elif 'stringValue' in cell['effectiveValue']:
                            row_values.append(cell['effectiveValue']['stringValue'])
                        else:
                            row_values.append(None)
                    else:
                        row_values.append(None)
            schedule_data.append(row_values)
        
        print(f"Loaded {len(schedule_data)} rows of schedule data")
        
        # Analyze back-to-back games
        print("Analyzing back-to-back games...")
        analysis_results = analyze_back_to_back_games(schedule_data)
        
        # Print summary
        print(f"\nFound {len(analysis_results)} teams")
        total_b2b_league = sum(team_data['Total'] for team_data in analysis_results.values())
        print(f"Total back-to-back sets across all teams: {total_b2b_league}")
        
        # Save to CSV
        csv_filename = '/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis.csv'
        save_results_to_csv(analysis_results, csv_filename)
        
        # Display top 10 teams with most back-to-back games
        print("\nTop 10 teams with most back-to-back games:")
        sorted_by_total = sorted(analysis_results.items(), key=lambda x: x[1]['Total'], reverse=True)
        for i, (team, data) in enumerate(sorted_by_total[:10]):
            print(f"{i+1:2d}. {team:<25} Total: {data['Total']:2d} (HA:{data['HA']}, AH:{data['AH']}, HH:{data['HH']}, AA:{data['AA']})")
        
        return analysis_results
        
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error: {e}")
        return None

if __name__ == "__main__":
    results = main()
```

```text workspace/analyze_nhl_b2b_v2.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
NHL Back-to-Back Games Analysis
Analyzes the 2024-2025 NHL schedule to identify back-to-back games for each team
"""

import json
import csv
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from collections import defaultdict

def parse_date_from_excel(date_value):
    """Convert Excel date serial number to datetime object"""
    if isinstance(date_value, (int, float)):
        # Excel date serial number (days since 1900-01-01, with 1900 incorrectly treated as leap year)
        base_date = datetime(1899, 12, 30)  # Excel epoch adjusted for the leap year bug
        return base_date + timedelta(days=date_value)
    elif isinstance(date_value, str):
        # Try to parse as date string
        try:
            return datetime.strptime(date_value, '%Y-%m-%d')
        except:
            return None
    return None

def extract_cell_value(cell):
    """Extract value from a Google Sheets cell object"""
    if 'effectiveValue' in cell:
        if 'numberValue' in cell['effectiveValue']:
            return cell['effectiveValue']['numberValue']
        elif 'stringValue' in cell['effectiveValue']:
            return cell['effectiveValue']['stringValue']
    return None

def analyze_back_to_back_games(schedule_data):
    """
    Analyze the schedule data to find back-to-back games for each team
    Back-to-back games are defined as games on consecutive days (exactly 1 day apart)
    """
    
    # Parse the schedule data
    games = []
    
    # Skip header row and process data
    for row_data in schedule_data[1:]:  # Skip header
        if not row_data or len(row_data) < 6:
            continue
            
        try:
            # Extract data from row (Date, Visitor, Home)
            date_val = extract_cell_value(row_data[0]) if len(row_data) > 0 else None
            visitor = extract_cell_value(row_data[3]) if len(row_data) > 3 else None  # Column D - Visitor
            home = extract_cell_value(row_data[5]) if len(row_data) > 5 else None     # Column F - Home
            
            if not date_val or not visitor or not home:
                continue
                
            # Parse date
            game_date = parse_date_from_excel(date_val)
            if not game_date:
                continue
                
            games.append({
                'date': game_date,
                'visitor': visitor,
                'home': home
            })
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error processing row: {e}")
            continue
    
    # Sort games by date
    games.sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])
    
    print(f"Processed {len(games)} games")
    print(f"Date range: {games[0]['date'].strftime('%Y-%m-%d')} to {games[-1]['date'].strftime('%Y-%m-%d')}")
    
    # Create team schedules
    team_schedules = defaultdict(list)
    
    for game in games:
        # Add game to visitor team's schedule (away game)
        team_schedules[game['visitor']].append({
            'date': game['date'],
            'location': 'away',
            'opponent': game['home']
        })
        
        # Add game to home team's schedule (home game)
        team_schedules[game['home']].append({
            'date': game['date'],
            'location': 'home',
            'opponent': game['visitor']
        })
    
    # Sort each team's schedule by date
    for team in team_schedules:
        team_schedules[team].sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])
    
    print(f"Found {len(team_schedules)} teams")
    
    # Find back-to-back games for each team
    b2b_analysis = {}
    
    for team, schedule in team_schedules.items():
        b2b_sets = {
            'HA': 0,  # Home-Away
            'AH': 0,  # Away-Home
            'HH': 0,  # Home-Home
            'AA': 0   # Away-Away
        }
        
        # Check consecutive games
        for i in range(len(schedule) - 1):
            current_game = schedule[i]
            next_game = schedule[i + 1]
            
            # Check if games are on consecutive days (exactly 1 day apart)
            date_diff = (next_game['date'] - current_game['date']).days
            
            if date_diff == 1:  # Back-to-back games
                # Determine the configuration
                current_loc = current_game['location'][0].upper()  # 'H' or 'A'
                next_loc = next_game['location'][0].upper()        # 'H' or 'A'
                
                config = current_loc + next_loc
                if config in b2b_sets:
                    b2b_sets[config] += 1
        
        # Calculate total
        total_b2b = sum(b2b_sets.values())
        
        b2b_analysis[team] = {
            'HA': b2b_sets['HA'],
            'AH': b2b_sets['AH'], 
            'HH': b2b_sets['HH'],
            'AA': b2b_sets['AA'],
            'Total': total_b2b
        }
    
    return b2b_analysis

def save_results_to_csv(analysis_results, filename):
    """Save the analysis results to a CSV file"""
    
    # Sort teams alphabetically
    sorted_teams = sorted(analysis_results.keys())
    
    with open(filename, 'w', newline='', encoding='utf-8') as csvfile:
        fieldnames = ['Team', 'HA', 'AH', 'HH', 'AA', 'Total']
        writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
        
        writer.writeheader()
        for team in sorted_teams:
            row = {'Team': team}
            row.update(analysis_results[team])
            writer.writerow(row)
    
    print(f"Results saved to {filename}")

def main():
    # Load the schedule data from the overlong tool output file
    try:
        with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/eXqvh5wAnj78xz5WSmnJ5t.json', 'r') as f:
            data = json.load(f)
        
        # Extract the sheet data
        sheet_data = data['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']
        
        print(f"Loaded {len(sheet_data)} rows of schedule data")
        
        # Analyze back-to-back games
        print("Analyzing back-to-back games...")
        analysis_results = analyze_back_to_back_games(sheet_data)
        
        # Print summary
        print(f"\nFound {len(analysis_results)} teams")
        total_b2b_league = sum(team_data['Total'] for team_data in analysis_results.values())
        print(f"Total back-to-back sets across all teams: {total_b2b_league}")
        
        # Save to CSV
        csv_filename = '/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis.csv'
        save_results_to_csv(analysis_results, csv_filename)
        
        # Display top 10 teams with most back-to-back games
        print("\nTop 10 teams with most back-to-back games:")
        sorted_by_total = sorted(analysis_results.items(), key=lambda x: x[1]['Total'], reverse=True)
        for i, (team, data) in enumerate(sorted_by_total[:10]):
            print(f"{i+1:2d}. {team:<25} Total: {data['Total']:2d} (HA:{data['HA']}, AH:{data['AH']}, HH:{data['HH']}, AA:{data['AA']})")
        
        # Show all teams
        print(f"\nAll teams back-to-back analysis:")
        print(f"{'Team':<25} {'HA':>3} {'AH':>3} {'HH':>3} {'AA':>3} {'Total':>5}")
        print("-" * 45)
        for team, data in sorted(analysis_results.items()):
            print(f"{team:<25} {data['HA']:3d} {data['AH']:3d} {data['HH']:3d} {data['AA']:3d} {data['Total']:5d}")
        
        return analysis_results
        
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error: {e}")
        import traceback
        traceback.print_exc()
        return None

if __name__ == "__main__":
    results = main()
```

```text workspace/analyze_nhl_b2b_v3.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
NHL Back-to-Back Games Analysis
Analyzes the 2024-2025 NHL schedule to identify back-to-back games for each team
"""

import json
import csv
from datetime import datetime, timedelta
from collections import defaultdict

def parse_date_from_excel(date_value):
    """Convert Excel date serial number to datetime object"""
    if isinstance(date_value, (int, float)):
        # Excel date serial number (days since 1900-01-01, with 1900 incorrectly treated as leap year)
        base_date = datetime(1899, 12, 30)  # Excel epoch adjusted for the leap year bug
        return base_date + timedelta(days=date_value)
    elif isinstance(date_value, str):
        # Try to parse as date string
        try:
            return datetime.strptime(date_value, '%Y-%m-%d')
        except:
            return None
    return None

def extract_cell_value(cell):
    """Extract value from a Google Sheets cell object"""
    if 'effectiveValue' in cell:
        if 'numberValue' in cell['effectiveValue']:
            return cell['effectiveValue']['numberValue']
        elif 'stringValue' in cell['effectiveValue']:
            return cell['effectiveValue']['stringValue']
    return None

def analyze_back_to_back_games(schedule_data):
    """
    Analyze the schedule data to find back-to-back games for each team
    Back-to-back games are defined as games on consecutive days (exactly 1 day apart)
    """
    
    # Parse the schedule data
    games = []
    
    # Skip header row and process data
    for row_data in schedule_data[1:]:  # Skip header
        if not row_data or 'values' not in row_data:
            continue
            
        try:
            values = row_data['values']
            if len(values) < 6:
                continue
                
            # Extract data from row (Date, Visitor, Home)
            date_val = extract_cell_value(values[0]) if len(values) > 0 else None
            visitor = extract_cell_value(values[3]) if len(values) > 3 else None  # Column D - Visitor
            home = extract_cell_value(values[5]) if len(values) > 5 else None     # Column F - Home
            
            if not date_val or not visitor or not home:
                continue
                
            # Parse date
            game_date = parse_date_from_excel(date_val)
            if not game_date:
                continue
                
            games.append({
                'date': game_date,
                'visitor': visitor,
                'home': home
            })
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"Error processing row: {e}")
            continue
    
    # Sort games by date
    games.sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])
    
    print(f"Processed {len(games)} games")
    if games:
        print(f"Date range: {games[0]['date'].strftime('%Y-%m-%d')} to {games[-1]['date'].strftime('%Y-%m-%d')}")
    
    # Create team schedules
    team_schedules = defaultdict(list)
    
    for game in games:
        # Add game to visitor team's schedule (away game)
        team_schedules[game['visitor']].append({
            'date': game['date'],
            'location': 'away',
            'opponent': game['home']
        })
        
        # Add game to home team's schedule (home game)
        team_schedules[game['home']].append({
            'date': game['date'],
            'location': 'home',
            'opponent': game['visitor']
        })
    
    # Sort each team's schedule by date
    for team in team_schedules:
        team_schedules[team].sort(key=lambda x: x['date'])
    
    print(f"Found {len(team_schedules)} teams")
    
    # Find back-to-back games for each team
    b2b_analysis = {}
    
    for team, schedule in team_schedules.items():
        b2b_sets = {
            'HA': 0,  # Home-Away
            'AH': 0,  # Away-Home
            'HH': 0,  # Home-Home
            'AA': 0   # Away-Away
        }
        
        # Check consecutive games
        for i in range(len(schedule) - 1):
            current_game = schedule[i]
            next_game = schedule[i + 1]
            
            # Check if games are on consecutive days (exactly 1 day apart)
            date_diff = (next_game['date'] - current_game['date']).days
            
            if date_diff == 1:  # Back-to-back games
                # Determine the configuration
                current_loc = current_game['location'][0].upper()  # 'H' or 'A'
                next_loc = next_game['location'][0].upper()        # 'H' or 'A'
                
                config = current_loc + next_loc
                if config in b2b_sets:
                    b2b_sets[config] += 1
        
        # Calculate total
        total_b2b = sum(b2b_sets.values())
        
        b2b_analysis[team] = {
            'HA': b2b_sets['HA'],
            'AH': b2b_sets['AH'], 
            'HH': b2b_sets['HH'],
            'AA': b2b_sets['AA'],
            'Total': total_b2b
        }
    
    return b2b_analysis

def save_results_to_csv(analysis_results, filename):
    """Save the analysis results to a CSV file"""
    
    # Sort teams alphabetically
    sorted_teams = sorted(analysis_results.keys())
    
    with open(filename, 'w', newline='', encoding='utf-8') as csvfile:
        fieldnames = ['Team', 'HA', 'AH', 'HH', 'AA', 'Total']
        writer = csv.DictWriter(csvfile, fieldnames=fieldnames)
        
        writer.writeheader()
        for team in sorted_teams:
            row = {'Team': team}
            row.update(analysis_results[team])
            writer.writerow(row)
    
    print(f"Results saved to {filename}")

def main():
    # Load the schedule data from the overlong tool output file
    try:
        with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/eXqvh5wAnj78xz5WSmnJ5t.json', 'r') as f:
            response_data = json.load(f)
        
        # The response is wrapped in a text field, so we need to parse the inner JSON
        inner_json = json.loads(response_data['text'])
        
        # Extract the sheet data
        sheet_data = inner_json['sheets'][0]['data'][0]['rowData']
        
        print(f"Loaded {len(sheet_data)} rows of schedule data")
        
        # Analyze back-to-back games
        print("Analyzing back-to-back games...")
        analysis_results = analyze_back_to_back_games(sheet_data)
        
        # Print summary
        print(f"\nFound {len(analysis_results)} teams")
        total_b2b_league = sum(team_data['Total'] for team_data in analysis_results.values())
        print(f"Total back-to-back sets across all teams: {total_b2b_league}")
        
        # Save to CSV
        csv_filename = '/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis.csv'
        save_results_to_csv(analysis_results, csv_filename)
        
        # Display top 10 teams with most back-to-back games
        print("\nTop 10 teams with most back-to-back games:")
        sorted_by_total = sorted(analysis_results.items(), key=lambda x: x[1]['Total'], reverse=True)
        for i, (team, data) in enumerate(sorted_by_total[:10]):
            print(f"{i+1:2d}. {team:<25} Total: {data['Total']:2d} (HA:{data['HA']}, AH:{data['AH']}, HH:{data['HH']}, AA:{data['AA']})")
        
        # Show all teams
        print(f"\nAll teams back-to-back analysis:")
        print(f"{'Team':<25} {'HA':>3} {'AH':>3} {'HH':>3} {'AA':>3} {'Total':>5}")
        print("-" * 45)
        for team, data in sorted(analysis_results.items()):
            print(f"{team:<25} {data['HA']:3d} {data['AH']:3d} {data['HH']:3d} {data['AA']:3d} {data['Total']:5d}")
        
        return analysis_results
        
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"Error: {e}")
        import traceback
        traceback.print_exc()
        return None

if __name__ == "__main__":
    results = main()
```

```text workspace/upload_to_sheets.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Upload NHL B2B analysis results to Google Sheets
"""

import csv

# Read the CSV file and prepare data for Google Sheets
data = []

# Read the CSV file
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis.csv', 'r') as f:
    reader = csv.reader(f)
    for row in reader:
        data.append(row)

print(f"Loaded {len(data)} rows of data")
print(f"Headers: {data[0]}")
print(f"First few rows:")
for i in range(min(5, len(data))):
    print(f"  {data[i]}")

# Convert to format expected by Google Sheets API
sheet_data = []
for row in data:
    sheet_row = []
    for cell in row:
        # Try to convert to number if possible
        try:
            if cell.isdigit():
                sheet_row.append(int(cell))
            else:
                sheet_row.append(cell)
        except:
            sheet_row.append(cell)
    sheet_data.append(sheet_row)

print(f"\nConverted data preview:")
for i in range(min(5, len(sheet_data))):
    print(f"  {sheet_data[i]}")

# Save the converted data
import json
with open('/workspace/dumps/workspace/sheet_data.json', 'w') as f:
    json.dump(sheet_data, f, indent=2)

print(f"\nSaved converted data to sheet_data.json")
```

<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 48 48" width="14px" height="14px" style={{margin: 0, padding: 0, display: 'inline-block'}}><path fill="#43a047" d="M37,45H11c-1.657,0-3-1.343-3-3V6c0-1.657,1.343-3,3-3h19l10,10v29C40,43.657,38.657,45,37,45z"/><path fill="#c8e6c9" d="M40 13L30 13 30 3z"/><path fill="#2e7d32" d="M30 13L40 23 40 13z"/><path fill="#e8f5e9" d="M31,23H17h-2v2v2v2v2v2v2v2h18v-2v-2v-2v-2v-2v-2v-2H31z M17,25h4v2h-4V25z M17,29h4v2h-4V29z M17,33h4v2h-4V33z M31,35h-8v-2h8V35z M31,31h-8v-2h8V31z M31,27h-8v-2h8V27z"/></svg> `google_sheet update_cells`

```text workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis_summary.md
# NHL 2024-2025 Back-to-Back Games Analysis

## Summary

This analysis examined the NHL 2024-2025 schedule to identify back-to-back games (games played on consecutive days) for each team. The analysis covers 1,312 games from October 4, 2024, to April 17, 2025.

## Key Findings

### League-Wide Statistics
- **Total back-to-back sets**: 398 across all 32 teams
- **Average per team**: 12.4 back-to-back sets
- **Date range analyzed**: October 4, 2024 - April 17, 2025
- **Total games analyzed**: 1,312 games

### Back-to-Back Configuration Types
- **HA (Home-Away)**: Home game followed by away game
- **AH (Away-Home)**: Away game followed by home game  
- **HH (Home-Home)**: Two consecutive home games
- **AA (Away-Away)**: Two consecutive away games

### Teams with Most Back-to-Back Games

| Rank | Team | Total | HA | AH | HH | AA |
|------|------|-------|----|----|----|----|
| 1 | Toronto Maple Leafs | 16 | 6 | 4 | 2 | 4 |
| 2 | Montreal Canadiens | 15 | 4 | 2 | 2 | 7 |
| 2 | Carolina Hurricanes | 15 | 2 | 1 | 5 | 7 |
| 4 | Florida Panthers | 14 | 1 | 4 | 2 | 7 |
| 4 | New York Rangers | 14 | 5 | 4 | 2 | 3 |
| 4 | Pittsburgh Penguins | 14 | 1 | 4 | 4 | 5 |
| 4 | Edmonton Oilers | 14 | 2 | 2 | 2 | 8 |
| 4 | Los Angeles Kings | 14 | 1 | 2 | 4 | 7 |
| 4 | Ottawa Senators | 14 | 3 | 3 | 3 | 5 |
| 4 | Nashville Predators | 14 | 2 | 2 | 1 | 9 |

### Teams with Fewest Back-to-Back Games

| Rank | Team | Total | HA | AH | HH | AA |
|------|------|-------|----|----|----|----|
| 1 | Winnipeg Jets | 8 | 1 | 2 | 1 | 4 |
| 2 | Boston Bruins | 10 | 4 | 4 | 0 | 2 |
| 2 | Calgary Flames | 10 | 3 | 0 | 0 | 7 |
| 2 | St. Louis Blues | 10 | 2 | 2 | 2 | 4 |
| 2 | Vancouver Canucks | 10 | 1 | 1 | 3 | 5 |

### Configuration Analysis

#### Away-Away (AA) Games
- Most demanding configuration (travel + fatigue)
- **Highest AA**: Nashville Predators (9), Anaheim Ducks (10)
- **Lowest AA**: Boston Bruins (2), Chicago Blackhawks (3)

#### Home-Away (HA) Games  
- Moderate difficulty (home comfort then travel)
- **Highest HA**: Columbus Blue Jackets (7), Toronto Maple Leafs (6)
- **Lowest HA**: Seattle Kraken (0), Multiple teams (1)

#### Away-Home (AH) Games
- Recovery advantage (travel then home comfort)
- **Highest AH**: New Jersey Devils (5), Multiple teams (4)
- **Lowest AH**: Multiple teams (0-1)

#### Home-Home (HH) Games
- Least demanding configuration
- **Highest HH**: Carolina Hurricanes (5), Los Angeles Kings (4)
- **Lowest HH**: Multiple teams (0)

## Coaching Implications

### High-Risk Teams (15+ B2B sets)
- **Toronto Maple Leafs** (16): Highest total, balanced across all configurations
- **Montreal Canadiens** (15): High AA burden (7 sets)
- **Carolina Hurricanes** (15): Unusual HH concentration (5 sets)

### Moderate-Risk Teams (12-14 B2B sets)
Most teams fall in this range, requiring standard rotation planning.

### Low-Risk Teams (8-11 B2B sets)
- **Winnipeg Jets** (8): Significant scheduling advantage
- **Boston Bruins** (10): Well-balanced, no HH games
- **Calgary Flames** (10): No AH or HH games

## Recommendations

1. **Priority Focus**: Teams with high AA counts need enhanced travel and recovery protocols
2. **Roster Management**: Teams with 14+ B2B sets should prioritize depth and rotation
3. **Recovery Planning**: AA and HA configurations require the most attention for player wellness
4. **Competitive Advantage**: Teams with fewer B2B sets (especially Winnipeg) have inherent scheduling advantages

## Files Generated

- `nhl_b2b_analysis.csv`: Complete analysis results
- Google Spreadsheet: "nhl_b2b_analysis" with sheet "NHL-B2B-Analysis"
- Spreadsheet ID: `1mYYYf4vv86UtF4gFWMSmJwccoVEcWaI6rHxfApRiNj0`

## Data Source
NHL 2024-2025 schedule data from Google Sheets (1,312 games analyzed)
```

### üìÅ **Files Created**

1. **Google Spreadsheet:** `nhl_b2b_analysis`
   - **Sheet name:** `NHL-B2B-Analysis`
   - **Spreadsheet ID:** `1mYYYf4vv86UtF4gFWMSmJwccoVEcWaI6rHxfApRiNj0`
   - **Headers:** Team, HA, AH, HH, AA, Total

2. **Local CSV file:** `/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis.csv`

3. **Detailed summary report:** `/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis_summary.md`

### üèí **Back-to-Back Configuration Types**
- **HA (Home-Away):** Home game followed by away game
- **AH (Away-Home):** Away game followed by home game  
- **HH (Home-Home):** Two consecutive home games (least demanding)
- **AA (Away-Away):** Two consecutive away games (most demanding)

### üéØ **Coaching Implications**
- **High-priority teams** (15+ B2B sets): Toronto, Montreal, Carolina
- **Away-Away burden leaders**: Nashville (9), Anaheim (10) - need enhanced recovery protocols
- **Scheduling advantage**: Winnipeg Jets with only 8 B2B sets

The analysis is now ready for your coaching staff to use for season-long conditioning and rotation planning. The Google Spreadsheet allows for easy sharing and collaboration, while the local CSV file provides a backup for your data analysts.

```text workspace/b2b_analysis.py

import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

# Load the schedule data
with open("/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/hngbMmtAb5poWFYK5EqW6M.json", "r") as f:
    raw_data = json.load(f)

# The actual data is nested inside the 'text' field and is a JSON string.
# So we need to parse it twice.
fixed_json_string = raw_data['text'].replace('\\n', '\n').replace('\\\"', '\"')

# Remove the outer '{\"type\":\"text\",\"text\":\"', and the trailing '\"}'
if fixed_json_string.startswith('{\"type\":\"text\",\"text\":\"'):
    fixed_json_string = fixed_json_string[len('{\"type\":\"text\",\"text\":\"'):-len('\"}')]

# Now, load the inner JSON string
schedule_data = json.loads(fixed_json_string)


# Extract row data
rows = schedule_data["sheets"][0]["data"][0]["rowData"]

# Get header
header = [cell.get("formattedValue", "") for cell in rows[0]["values"]]

# Parse rows
games = []
for row in rows[1:]:
    game_data = {}
    for i, cell in enumerate(row["values"]):
        game_data[header[i]] = cell.get("formattedValue", None)
    games.append(game_data)

# Get all unique team names
teams = set()
for game in games:
    teams.add(game["Visitor"])
    teams.add(game["Home"])

# Initialize a dictionary to store each team's schedule
team_schedules = {team: [] for team in teams}
for game in games:
    if game["Date"] and (game["Visitor"] in team_schedules) and (game["Home"] in team_schedules):
        team_schedules[game["Visitor"]].append({"date": game["Date"], "location": "Away"})
        team_schedules[game["Home"]].append({"date": game["Date"], "location": "Home"})

# Initialize a dictionary to store back-to-back counts
b2b_counts = {team: {"HA": 0, "AH": 0, "HH": 0, "AA": 0, "Total": 0} for team in teams}

# Identify and categorize back-to-back games
for team, schedule in team_schedules.items():
    # Sort the schedule by date
    schedule.sort(key=lambda x: datetime.strptime(x["date"], "%Y-%m-%d"))
    for i in range(len(schedule) - 1):
        date1 = datetime.strptime(schedule[i]["date"], "%Y-%m-%d")
        date2 = datetime.strptime(schedule[i+1]["date"], "%Y-%m-%d")
        if date2 - date1 == timedelta(days=1):
            loc1 = schedule[i]["location"]
            loc2 = schedule[i+1]["location"]
            if loc1 == "Home" and loc2 == "Away":
                b2b_counts[team]["HA"] += 1
            elif loc1 == "Away" and loc2 == "Home":
                b2b_counts[team]["AH"] += 1
            elif loc1 == "Home" and loc2 == "Home":
                b2b_counts[team]["HH"] += 1
            elif loc1 == "Away" and loc2 == "Away":
                b2b_counts[team]["AA"] += 1
            b2b_counts[team]["Total"] += 1

# Prepare the data for CSV and Google Sheet
output_data = [["Team", "HA", "AH", "HH", "AA", "Total"]]
for team in sorted(b2b_counts.keys()):
    counts = b2b_counts[team]
    output_data.append([team, counts["HA"], counts["AH"], counts["HH"], counts["AA"], counts["Total"]])

# Save to CSV
import csv
with open("/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis.csv", "w", newline="") as f:
    writer = csv.writer(f)
    writer.writerows(output_data)

# Prepare for Google Sheet
# The sheet and folder are already created, just need to write the data.
print(json.dumps(output_data))


```

```text workspace/b2b_analysis.py
# Load the schedule data
with open("/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/hngbMmtAb5poWFYK5EqW6M.json", "r") as f:
    raw_data = json.load(f)

# So we need to parse it twice.

    writer = csv.writer(f)
    writer.writerows(output_data)

# Prepare for Google Sheet
# The sheet and folder are already created, just need to write the data.
print(json.dumps(output_data))
```

```text workspace/b2b_analysis.py

import json
from datetime import datetime, timedelta

# Load the schedule data
with open("/workspace/dumps/workspace/.overlong_tool_outputs/hngbMmtAb5poWFYK5EqW6M.json", "r") as f:
    raw_data = json.load(f)

# The actual data is a JSON string within the 'text' field of another JSON string.
schedule_data = json.loads(json.loads(raw_data['text'])['text'])

# Extract row data
rows = schedule_data["sheets"][0]["data"][0]["rowData"]

# Get header
header = [cell.get("formattedValue", "") for cell in rows[0]["values"]]

# Parse rows
games = []
for row in rows[1:]:
    game_data = {}
    if "values" in row:
        for i, cell in enumerate(row["values"]):
            if i < len(header):
                game_data[header[i]] = cell.get("formattedValue", None)
    if game_data:
        games.append(game_data)


# Get all unique team names
teams = set()
for game in games:
    if game.get("Visitor") and game.get("Home"):
        teams.add(game["Visitor"])
        teams.add(game["Home"])

# Initialize a dictionary to store each team's schedule
team_schedules = {team: [] for team in teams}
for game in games:
    if game.get("Date") and game.get("Visitor") in team_schedules and game.get("Home") in team_schedules:
        team_schedules[game["Visitor"]].append({"date": game["Date"], "location": "Away"})
        team_schedules[game["Home"]].append({"date": game["Date"], "location": "Home"})

# Initialize a dictionary to store back-to-back counts
b2b_counts = {team: {"HA": 0, "AH": 0, "HH": 0, "AA": 0, "Total": 0} for team in teams}

# Identify and categorize back-to-back games
for team, schedule in team_schedules.items():
    if not schedule:
        continue
    # Sort the schedule by date
    schedule.sort(key=lambda x: datetime.strptime(x["date"], "%Y-%m-%d"))
    for i in range(len(schedule) - 1):
        try:
            date1 = datetime.strptime(schedule[i]["date"], "%Y-%m-%d")
            date2 = datetime.strptime(schedule[i+1]["date"], "%Y-%m-%d")
            if date2 - date1 == timedelta(days=1):
                loc1 = schedule[i]["location"]
                loc2 = schedule[i+1]["location"]
                if loc1 == "Home" and loc2 == "Away":
                    b2b_counts[team]["HA"] += 1
                elif loc1 == "Away" and loc2 == "Home":
                    b2b_counts[team]["AH"] += 1
                elif loc1 == "Home" and loc2 == "Home":
                    b2b_counts[team]["HH"] += 1
                elif loc1 == "Away" and loc2 == "Away":
                    b2b_counts[team]["AA"] += 1
                b2b_counts[team]["Total"] += 1
        except (ValueError, KeyError) as e:
            # Handle cases where date is not in the expected format or a key is missing
            print(f"Skipping a game for team {team} due to data issue: {e}")
            continue

# Prepare the data for CSV and Google Sheet
output_data = [["Team", "HA", "AH", "HH", "AA", "Total"]]
# Sort teams alphabetically, but handle the case where a team might not have any games
for team in sorted([t for t in b2b_counts.keys() if t]):
    counts = b2b_counts[team]
    output_data.append([team, counts["HA"], counts["AH"], counts["HH"], counts["AA"], counts["Total"]])

# Save to CSV
import csv
with open("/workspace/dumps/workspace/nhl_b2b_analysis.csv", "w", newline="") as f:
    writer = csv.writer(f)
    writer.writerows(output_data)

# Prepare for Google Sheet
print(json.dumps(output_data))

```

<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"  viewBox="0 0 48 48" width="14px" height="14px" style={{margin: 0, padding: 0, display: 'inline-block'}}><path fill="#0277bd" d="M19.847,41.956c-5.629-0.002-11.259,0.024-16.888-0.013c-2.855-0.019-3.374-0.7-2.731-3.525 c2.178-9.58,4.427-19.143,6.557-28.734C7.356,7.112,8.588,5.975,11.312,6C22.57,6.106,33.829,6.034,45.088,6.046 c2.824,0.003,3.298,0.614,2.664,3.511c-2.058,9.406-4.129,18.809-6.236,28.203c-0.789,3.516-1.697,4.187-5.353,4.195 C30.724,41.966,25.285,41.958,19.847,41.956z"/><path fill="#fafafa" d="M25.057 23.922c-.608-.687-1.114-1.267-1.531-1.732-2.43-2.728-4.656-5.27-7.063-7.869-1.102-1.189-1.453-2.344-.13-3.518 1.307-1.16 2.592-1.058 3.791.277 3.34 3.717 6.676 7.438 10.071 11.104 1.268 1.369.972 2.3-.424 3.315-5.359 3.895-10.687 7.833-16.01 11.778-1.196.887-2.337 1.109-3.304-.201-1.066-1.445-.08-2.305 1.026-3.114 3.955-2.893 7.903-5.798 11.834-8.725C23.865 24.83 24.595 24.267 25.057 23.922zM21.75 37C20.625 37 20 36 20 35s.625-2 1.75-2c4.224 0 6.112 0 9.5 0 1.125 0 1.75 1 1.75 2s-.625 2-1.75 2C29.125 37 25 37 21.75 37z"/></svg> `terminal run_command`
